Cause and Conditions for Shuf'ah: Valid Sale and Ishhad
Defines the cause and conditions of shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the cause (sabab) from the condition (shart) for shuf'ah, and explain the requirements of valid sale, absence of seller's option, and the need for witnessing (ishhad).

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is triggered by a valid sale free from seller's option; its right is stabilized only through witnessing.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the foundational rules of shuf'ah. It corrects a common misunderstanding by distinguishing the true cause (permanent property connection) from the condition (valid sale), and then discusses additional conditions and the procedural requirement of ishhad. Understanding these elements is essential for correctly applying the right of pre-emption in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify cause vs. condition
The text first notes that some scholars considered the sale itself as the cause of shuf'ah, but the correct view is that the cause is the permanent connection of properties (ittisal al-amlak 'ala al-luzum), and sale is a condition (shart) for its activation.
This distinction affects when the right arises.
2
Examine the condition of valid sale
The passage explains that the sale must be valid (sahih); an invalid (fasid) sale does not trigger shuf'ah because it does not definitively transfer ownership. Explain the reasoning: before possession it conveys no ownership, and after possession it is subject to annulment.
If the annulment is dropped, shuf'ah becomes obligatory.
3
Understand the seller's option impediment
A condition is that the sale must be free from the seller's option (khiyar al-ba'i'), because the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership. The buyer's option and other options (inspection, defect) do not impede shuf'ah.
Contrast between seller's option (impediment) and buyer's option (not an impediment).
4
Recognize the need for ishhad
The right of shuf'ah is weak; it can be lost by neglect. Therefore, to stabilize it, the claimant must perform immediate demand (talab al-muwathabah) upon hearing the sale, and then prove that demand through witnessing (ishhad) before a judge.
Without ishhad, the right may not be enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالبيع: تتعلق أيضا بقوله: "تجب للخليط"، وأشار بهذا إلى أن الشفعة البيع، أعني بيع الدار المشفوعة، سبب وجوب هكذا قال بعضهم، والصحيح أن السبب هو اتصال الأملاك على اللزوم، والبيع شرط، فحينئذ يكون التقدير: تجب الشفعة بعقد البيع أي بعد وجوده والمراد بالبيع الصحيح، فإن البيع الفاسد لا تجب فيه الشفعة؛ لأنه قبل القبض لا يفيد الملك، وبعده مستحق للفسخ، فإيجابها تقرير الفساد، فلا يجوز إلا إذا سقط الفسخ وجبت؛ لزوال المانع، وفيه قيد آخر، أن يكون خاليا عن خيار البائع؛ لأنه يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملكه حتى لو أسقطه وجبت، وخيار المشتري غير مانع، لأنه لا يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملك البائع، وكذلك خيار الرؤية والعيب لا يمنعان. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وتستقر بالإشهاد : أي تستقر الشفعة بالإشهاد؛ لأنها حق ضعيف يبطل بالإعراض، فلابد من الإشهاد بعد طلب المواثبة للاستقرار، كما أنه لابد من طلب المواثبة للاستقرار وهو أن يطلب كما سمع؛ ولأنه يحتاج إلى إثبات طلبه عند القاضي، ولا يمكنه ذلك إلا بالإشهاد. (فتح)
'By sale' is also attached to his statement: 'It is obligatory for the khalit.' And he indicated by this that pre-emption [is caused by] sale, specifically the sale of the house subject to pre-emption, is the cause of obligation—this is what some said. But the correct [view] is that the cause is the connection of properties in a permanent manner, and sale is a condition. So then the estimation is: pre-emption is obligatory by the contract of sale, i.e., after its existence. And what is meant by sale is the valid sale, because the invalid (fasid) sale does not obligate pre-emption; because before possession it does not confer ownership, and after possession it is subject to annulment, so imposing pre-emption would be confirming the invalidity, so it is not permissible unless the annulment is dropped and then it becomes obligatory due to the removal of the impediment. And in it is another condition: that it be free from the seller's option (khiyar al-ba'i'), because it prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership; even if he drops it, it becomes obligatory. The buyer's option is not an impediment because it does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership. Similarly, the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) and the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) are not impediments. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/335) 'And it stabilizes by witnessing (ishhad)': i.e., shuf'ah stabilizes by ishhad, because it is a weak right that is invalidated by turning away. So ishhad is necessary after the immediate demand (talab al-muwathabah) for stabilization, just as the immediate demand is necessary for stabilization, which is that he demand as soon as he hears [the sale]. And because he needs to prove his demand before the judge, and he cannot do that except by ishhad. (Fath)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage clarifies the cause (sabab) of shuf'ah. Some said the cause is the sale itself, but the correct view (al-sahih) is that the cause is the permanent connection of properties (ittisal al-amlak 'ala al-luzum), and sale is merely a condition (shart) for its activation. So shuf'ah becomes obligatory upon the existence of a valid sale contract (al-bay' al-sahih). An invalid sale (fassid) does not trigger shuf'ah because before possession it does not transfer ownership, and after possession it is subject to annulment; imposing shuf'ah would mean confirming the invalid transaction, which is impermissible. However, if the annulment is dropped (e.g., by the parties agreeing), then shuf'ah becomes obligatory. Another condition is that the sale must be free from the seller's option (khiyar al-ba'i'), because the seller's option delays the transfer of ownership; if the seller drops it, shuf'ah applies. The buyer's option, the option of inspection, and the option of defect do not impede shuf'ah because they do not prevent the seller's ownership from leaving. Finally, the right of shuf'ah is a weak right that is lost if the claimant shows disregard. Therefore, to stabilize it, the claimant must perform two things: first, immediate demand (talab al-muwathabah) upon hearing the sale; second, witnessing (ishhad) to prove the demand before a judge. Without ishhad, the right may not be enforced.

Key Terms
سبب الوجوب (sabab al-wujub): The cause of obligation; here the permanent connection of properties.
البيع الصحيح (al-bay' al-sahih): Valid sale that transfers ownership definitively.
خيار البائع (khiyar al-ba'i'): The seller's option to rescind the sale; impedes shuf'ah until dropped.
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Witnessing the demand of shuf'ah to stabilize the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The permanent connection of properties is the cause, and sale is a condition

D) The cause is the buyer's acceptance

Key Takeaway
The right of shuf'ah arises from permanent property connection, is conditioned on a valid sale free from seller's option, and is stabilized through immediate demand and witnessing.

Who Qualifies for Pre-emption: Neighbor vs Co-owner
Commentary on matn ruling about neighbor pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a co-owner and an abutting neighbor for the purpose of shuf'ah and state the Hanafi rules for entitlement.

Core Idea
An abutting neighbor has pre-emption, but a co-owner in the same house is prioritized.

The right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is not granted to every neighbor; the Hanafi school carefully defines who qualifies. This lesson unpacks the commentary's distinction between a co-owner in the property itself and a mere abutting neighbor who shares only a wall or beams. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly applying shuf'ah in real property disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of claimants mentioned
Read the text's discussion of 'the one who places beams on the wall' and 'the partner in a beam on the wall.' Distinguish between co-ownership in the real estate and mere adjacency.
The commentary explicitly states that placing beams does not create partnership in the house.
2
Explain why placing beams does not create co-ownership
The wood (khashab) is movable property; partnership in movable property does not confer co-ownership in the real estate. Thus the person is only a neighbor (jār) through physical adjacency.
Contrast with partnership in the building and land together, which does create co-ownership.
3
Determine the priority order
Co-owners in the sold property itself are prioritized over abutting neighbors. The neighbor's right is subsidiary. Also, a neighbor who is a partner only in a wall does not get priority over other abutting neighbors.
The text: 'ولا يترجح بذلك على غيره من الجيران' – he is not given preference over other neighbors.
4
Summarize the rule for entitlement
Only co-owners in the real estate (same property) and abutting neighbors (jār mulāṣiq) are entitled. Partnership in movable or in building without land does not confer shuf'ah.
This is a Hanafi specific ruling; other schools may have different definitions.

وواضع الجذوع على الحائط والشريك في خشبة على الحائط جار على عدد الرؤوس بالبيع، وتستقر بالإشهاد وقد روي هذا التفسير مرفوعا، "أثبت النبي الله الشفعة للجار بعلة قربه فيستحق الشفعة"، وحديث جابره معناه: أنها لا تجب للجار بقسمة الشركاء؛ لأنهم أحق به منه وحقه متأخر عن حقهم، وبذلك يحصل التوفيق بين الأحاديث. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٤/٢] (فتح) وواضع الجذوع إلخ : أي واضع الجذوع على الحائط، والشريك في خشبة موضوعة على الحائط جار، فلا يستحق الشفعة إلا بعد الشريك في نفس المبيع والشريك في حق المبيع؛ لأن الشركة المعتبرة هي الشركة في العقار، لا في المنقول والخشبة منقولة، وبوضع الجذوع على الحائط لا يصير شريكا في الدار، وكذا بالشركة في الجذوع لا يكون شريكا فيها، ولكنه جار ملاصق لوجود اتصال بقعة أحدهما ببقعة الآخر، فيستحق الآخر الشفعة على أنه جار ملاصق، ولا يترجح بذلك على غيره من الجيران، وكذا إذا كان بعض الجيران شريكا في الجدار، لا يقدم على غيره من الجيران؛ لأن الشركة في البناء المجرد بدون الأرض لا يستحق بها الشفعة، ولو كان البناء والمكان الذي عليه البناء مشتركا بينهما كان هو أولى من غيره من الجيران رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٤/٢] على عدد الرؤوس: كلمة "على" متعلقة بقوله: "تجب للخليط" أي تجب الشفعة على عدد الرؤوس، وقال الشافعي على قدر سهامهم و به قال مالك وأحمد، كما إذا كانت دار بين ثلاثة لأحدهم نصفها، وللآخر سدسها، وللآخر ثلثها، فباع صاحب السدس سدسه فطلب الدار بالشفعة فإنها تقسم بينهما أخماسا: ثلاثة أخماس لصاحب النصف، والخمسان لصاحب الثلث؛ لأن الشفعة من مرافق الملك، فأشبه الربح، ولنا: أن العلة اتصال الملك، وقليله في ذلك ككثيره، فيكون ما باع صاحب السدس بينهما نصفان. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وهو بالبيع: تتعلق أيضا بقوله: "تجب للخليط"، وأشار بهذا إلى أن الشفعة البيع، أعني بيع الدار المشفوعة، سبب وجوب هكذا قال بعضهم، والصحيح أن السبب هو اتصال الأملاك على اللزوم، والبيع شرط، فحينئذ يكون التقدير: تجب الشفعة بعقد البيع أي بعد وجوده والمراد بالبيع الصحيح، فإن البيع الفاسد لا تجب فيه الشفعة؛ لأنه قبل القبض لا يفيد الملك، وبعده مستحق للفسخ، فإيجابها تقرير الفساد، فلا يجوز إلا إذا سقط الفسخ وجبت؛ لزوال المانع، وفيه قيد آخر، أن يكون خاليا عن خيار البائع؛ لأنه يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملكه حتى لو أسقطه وجبت، وخيار المشتري غير مانع، لأنه لا يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملك البائع، وكذلك خيار الرؤية والعيب لا يمنعان. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وتستقر بالإشهاد : أي تستقر الشفعة بالإشهاد؛ لأنها حق ضعيف يبطل بالإعراض، فلابد من الإشهاد بعد طلب المواثبة للاستقرار، كما أنه لابد من طلب المواثبة للاستقرار وهو أن يطلب كما سمع؛ ولأنه يحتاج إلى إثبات طلبه عند القاضي، ولا يمكنه ذلك إلا بالإشهاد. (فتح)
And the one who places beams on the wall and the partner in a beam on the wall is a neighbor (pre-emptor) according to the number of heads through sale, and it is confirmed by bearing witness. And this interpretation has been reported as marfu': 'The Prophet established pre-emption for the neighbor due to the cause of his proximity, so he deserves pre-emption.' And the hadith of Jabir means: It is not obligatory for the neighbor by the division of partners; because they are more entitled to it than him, and his right is subsequent to their right. And by that, reconciliation between the hadiths is achieved. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/334) (Fath) 'And the one who places beams etc.': i.e., the one who places beams on the wall, and the partner in a beam placed on the wall, is a neighbor, so he does not deserve pre-emption except after the partner in the very thing sold and the partner in the right of the thing sold; because the considered partnership is partnership in real estate, not in movable property, and wood is movable, and by placing beams on the wall he does not become a partner in the house, and likewise by partnership in beams he does not become a partner in it. But he is an abutting neighbor due to the existence of connection of one's plot with the other's plot, so he deserves pre-emption as an abutting neighbor, and he is not given preference thereby over other neighbors. Likewise if some of the neighbors are partners in the wall, he is not given precedence over other neighbors; because partnership in the mere building without land does not entitle one to pre-emption. If the building and the place on which the building is were shared between them, then he would be more entitled than other neighbors. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/334) 'According to the number of heads': The word 'according to' is attached to His saying: 'It is obligatory for the partner' i.e., pre-emption is obligatory according to the number of heads. And al-Shafi'i said: according to the measure of their shares, and Malik and Ahmad agreed with him. For example, if there is a house among three: one has half, another has one-sixth, and another has one-third. Then the owner of the sixth sells his sixth, and the two others seek pre-emption. It is divided among them in fifths: three fifths for the owner of half, and two fifths for the owner of the third; because pre-emption is among the appurtenances of ownership, so it resembles profit. And our proof: the cause is connection of ownership, and a little of it in that regard is like much of it. So what the owner of the sixth sold is half between them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/335) 'Through sale': It is also attached to His saying: 'It is obligatory for the partner.' And he indicated by this that pre-emption by sale, i.e., selling the house subject to pre-emption, is the cause of obligation; thus said some. And the correct view is that the cause is the connection of properties permanently, and sale is a condition. Then the estimate is: pre-emption is obligatory by the contract of sale, i.e., after its existence. And by 'sale' is meant the valid sale, for pre-emption is not obligatory in a defective sale; because before delivery it does not confer ownership, and after it is subject to rescission, so making it obligatory would confirm the defect, so it is not permissible unless when rescission falls and it becomes obligatory due to removal of the impediment. And in it is another restriction: that it be free from the seller's option; because it prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership, so if he drops it, it becomes obligatory. And the buyer's option is not an impediment because it does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership. Likewise the options of inspection and defect do not prevent. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/335) 'And it is confirmed by bearing witness': i.e., pre-emption is confirmed by bearing witness; because it is a weak right that is nullified by disregard. So bearing witness is necessary after the immediate demand for confirmation, just as the immediate demand is necessary for confirmation – that he demand as soon as he hears. And because he needs to prove his demand before the judge, and he cannot do so except by bearing witness. (Fath)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding pre-emption (shuf'ah). It begins by defining who qualifies as a 'neighbor' (jar) for the purpose of shuf'ah: a person who places his beams on another's wall, or who shares a beam on a wall, is considered a neighbor but not a co-owner. As an abutting neighbor, he is entitled to shuf'ah but does not get priority over other neighbors. The commentary then explains the famous ruling that shuf'ah is distributed among co-owners on the basis of heads, not shares. This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who distributes according to share proportions. The Hanafi proof is that the effective cause ('illa) for shuf'ah is the connection of ownership (ittisal al-milk), and the extent of one's share does not affect this connection. The passage also clarifies that the sale must be valid and free from options that prevent transfer of ownership (like seller's option), while buyer's options do not impede. Finally, it discusses the need for bearing witness (ishhad) to confirm the right of shuf'ah, because it is a weak right that can be lost through negligence.

Key Terms
جار ملاصق (jār mulāṣiq): Abutting neighbor whose property physically touches the sold property.
شركة في العقار (sharika fī al-ʿiqār): Partnership in real estate (land and building).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is entitled to shuf'ah?
A) A person who shares a wall with the sold property (abutting neighbor).
B) A person who owns a beam placed on the sold property's wall.
C) A person who is a co-owner in the building but not the land.
D) Both A and B, but C only if the building and land are shared.

Key Takeaway
An abutting neighbor has shuf'ah rights, but a co-owner in the real estate is given priority; mere partnership in a wall or beam does not create co-ownership.

Distribution of Pre-emption: Heads vs Shares
Commentary on matn ruling about distribution of shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that shuf'ah is distributed by heads and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is based on connection, not profit; equal heads, not proportional shares.

One of the most debated issues in shuf'ah is how to divide the pre-empted property among multiple eligible claimants. The Hanafi school holds that distribution is by number of heads (equally), while the Shafi'i school distributes by share value. This lesson dissects the proofs for each view and reveals the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The text states: 'تجب الشفعة على عدد الرؤوس' – pre-emption is obligatory according to the number of heads. This means all co-owners who are equally entitled to shuf'ah get equal shares regardless of their ownership proportion.
Example from the text: two co-owners with half and third get equal half each of the sold sixth.
2
Present the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik and Ahmad) hold that distribution is according to the measure of shares (على قدر سهامهم). Reason: shuf'ah is an appurtenance of ownership (مرافق الملك), so it should follow profit distribution.
The text gives the same example: owner of half gets 3/5, owner of third gets 2/5 of the sold sixth.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The effective cause ('illa) for shuf'ah is connection of ownership (اتصال الملك). This cause is the same for all co-owners, whether their shares are large or small. 'A little of it is like much of it.' Therefore, distribution is equal.
The hadith 'أثبت النبي الشفعة للجار بعلة قربه' supports that the cause is proximity, not share size.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If two co-owners have unequal shares (e.g., ½ and ⅓) and a third sells his ⅙, under Hanafi each gets half of that ⅙ (equal). Under Shafi'i, the owner of half gets 3/5, owner of third gets 2/5.
This affects the final distribution of the property among the pre-emptors.
5
Conclude with tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. The matn itself ('على عدد الرؤوس') is the relied-upon ruling. The commentary endorses it as 'our proof' (لنا).
The later Hanafi masters (like al-Marghinani) confirm this as the correct view.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding pre-emption (shuf'ah). It begins by defining who qualifies as a 'neighbor' (jar) for the purpose of shuf'ah: a person who places his beams on another's wall, or who shares a beam on a wall, is considered a neighbor but not a co-owner. As an abutting neighbor, he is entitled to shuf'ah but does not get priority over other neighbors. The commentary then explains the famous ruling that shuf'ah is distributed among co-owners on the basis of heads, not shares. This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who distributes according to share proportions. The Hanafi proof is that the effective cause ('illa) for shuf'ah is the connection of ownership (ittisal al-milk), and the extent of one's share does not affect this connection. The passage also clarifies that the sale must be valid and free from options that prevent transfer of ownership (like seller's option), while buyer's options do not impede. Finally, it discusses the need for bearing witness (ishhad) to confirm the right of shuf'ah, because it is a weak right that can be lost through negligence.

Key Terms
عدد الرؤوس (ʿadad al-ru'ūs): Distribution by heads (equal per person).
على قدر سهامهم (ʿalā qadr sihāmihim): According to the measure of their shares.

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, two co-owners have equal right of pre-emption. One owns 2/3, the other 1/3. The third co-owner sells his 1/4 share. How is the sold share divided between the two?
A) The 2/3 owner gets 2/3 of the sold share, the 1/3 owner gets 1/3.
B) Each gets half of the sold share.
C) The sold share is divided in proportion to ownership: 2/3 and 1/3.
D) Pre-emption only applies if they are equal owners.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's distribution of shuf'ah by heads, not shares, is based on the uniform nature of the cause (connection of ownership).

Conditions for Obligating Shuf'ah and Its Confirmation
Commentary on matn ruling about conditions and confirmation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that must be present for shuf'ah to be obligatory and explain the requirement of bearing witness.

Core Idea
Valid sale without seller's option and immediate demand with witnesses are pillars of shuf'ah.

Pre-emption is not an automatic right; it becomes obligatory only under specific conditions. This lesson unpacks the commentary's discussion on the cause vs condition, the effect of seller's and buyer's options, and the critical role of bearing witness (ishhad) to solidify the weak right. Proper application prevents the loss of shuf'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause vs condition for shuf'ah
The text distinguishes between the cause (sabab) and condition (shart). The correct view: the cause is permanent connection of properties (ittisāl al-milk ʿalā al-luzūm), and the sale is a condition for its activation.
Some earlier scholars said sale is the cause, but the commentator corrects this.
2
Explain why sale must be valid
A defective sale (fasid) does not confer ownership before delivery, and after delivery it is subject to rescission. Imposing shuf'ah would perpetuate the defect. Therefore, shuf'ah only arises from a valid sale.
Exception: if the defect is removed (e.g., waiver of rescission), then shuf'ah becomes obligatory.
3
Distinguish effects of seller's option vs buyer's option
Seller's option (khiyār al-bā'iʿ) prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership, so shuf'ah does not arise until the option is dropped. In contrast, buyer's option (khiyār al-mushtari) does not impede the transfer from seller's side; thus shuf'ah is not delayed.
Similarly, options of inspection (khiyār al-ru'ya) and defect (khiyār al-ʿayb) do not prevent.
4
Understand the role of bearing witness (ishhad)
Shuf'ah is a weak right (ḥaqq ḍaʿīf) that is nullified by disregard. Therefore, after immediate demand (ṭalab al-muwāthaba), the pre-emptor must have witnesses to testify to his claim. This is essential for proving his case before a judge.
Without ishhad, the right is not confirmed and can be lost.

وواضع الجذوع على الحائط والشريك في خشبة على الحائط جار على عدد الرؤوس بالبيع، وتستقر بالإشهاد وقد روي هذا التفسير مرفوعا، "أثبت النبي الله الشفعة للجار بعلة قربه فيستحق الشفعة"، وحديث جابره معناه: أنها لا تجب للجار بقسمة الشركاء؛ لأنهم أحق به منه وحقه متأخر عن حقهم، وبذلك يحصل التوفيق بين الأحاديث. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٤/٢] (فتح) وواضع الجذوع إلخ : أي واضع الجذوع على الحائط، والشريك في خشبة موضوعة على الحائط جار، فلا يستحق الشفعة إلا بعد الشريك في نفس المبيع والشريك في حق المبيع؛ لأن الشركة المعتبرة هي الشركة في العقار، لا في المنقول والخشبة منقولة، وبوضع الجذوع على الحائط لا يصير شريكا في الدار، وكذا بالشركة في الجذوع لا يكون شريكا فيها، ولكنه جار ملاصق لوجود اتصال بقعة أحدهما ببقعة الآخر، فيستحق الآخر الشفعة على أنه جار ملاصق، ولا يترجح بذلك على غيره من الجيران، وكذا إذا كان بعض الجيران شريكا في الجدار، لا يقدم على غيره من الجيران؛ لأن الشركة في البناء المجرد بدون الأرض لا يستحق بها الشفعة، ولو كان البناء والمكان الذي عليه البناء مشتركا بينهما كان هو أولى من غيره من الجيران رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٤/٢] على عدد الرؤوس: كلمة "على" متعلقة بقوله: "تجب للخليط" أي تجب الشفعة على عدد الرؤوس، وقال الشافعي على قدر سهامهم و به قال مالك وأحمد، كما إذا كانت دار بين ثلاثة لأحدهم نصفها، وللآخر سدسها، وللآخر ثلثها، فباع صاحب السدس سدسه فطلب الدار بالشفعة فإنها تقسم بينهما أخماسا: ثلاثة أخماس لصاحب النصف، والخمسان لصاحب الثلث؛ لأن الشفعة من مرافق الملك، فأشبه الربح، ولنا: أن العلة اتصال الملك، وقليله في ذلك ككثيره، فيكون ما باع صاحب السدس بينهما نصفان. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وهو بالبيع: تتعلق أيضا بقوله: "تجب للخليط"، وأشار بهذا إلى أن الشفعة البيع، أعني بيع الدار المشفوعة، سبب وجوب هكذا قال بعضهم، والصحيح أن السبب هو اتصال الأملاك على اللزوم، والبيع شرط، فحينئذ يكون التقدير: تجب الشفعة بعقد البيع أي بعد وجوده والمراد بالبيع الصحيح، فإن البيع الفاسد لا تجب فيه الشفعة؛ لأنه قبل القبض لا يفيد الملك، وبعده مستحق للفسخ، فإيجابها تقرير الفساد، فلا يجوز إلا إذا سقط الفسخ وجبت؛ لزوال المانع، وفيه قيد آخر، أن يكون خاليا عن خيار البائع؛ لأنه يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملكه حتى لو أسقطه وجبت، وخيار المشتري غير مانع، لأنه لا يمنع خروج المبيع عن ملك البائع، وكذلك خيار الرؤية والعيب لا يمنعان. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وتستقر بالإشهاد : أي تستقر الشفعة بالإشهاد؛ لأنها حق ضعيف يبطل بالإعراض، فلابد من الإشهاد بعد طلب المواثبة للاستقرار، كما أنه لابد من طلب المواثبة للاستقرار وهو أن يطلب كما سمع؛ ولأنه يحتاج إلى إثبات طلبه عند القاضي، ولا يمكنه ذلك إلا بالإشهاد. (فتح)
And the one who places beams on the wall and the partner in a beam on the wall is a neighbor (pre-emptor) according to the number of heads through sale, and it is confirmed by bearing witness. And this interpretation has been reported as marfu': 'The Prophet established pre-emption for the neighbor due to the cause of his proximity, so he deserves pre-emption.' And the hadith of Jabir means: It is not obligatory for the neighbor by the division of partners; because they are more entitled to it than him, and his right is subsequent to their right. And by that, reconciliation between the hadiths is achieved. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/334) (Fath) 'And the one who places beams etc.': i.e., the one who places beams on the wall, and the partner in a beam placed on the wall, is a neighbor, so he does not deserve pre-emption except after the partner in the very thing sold and the partner in the right of the thing sold; because the considered partnership is partnership in real estate, not in movable property, and wood is movable, and by placing beams on the wall he does not become a partner in the house, and likewise by partnership in beams he does not become a partner in it. But he is an abutting neighbor due to the existence of connection of one's plot with the other's plot, so he deserves pre-emption as an abutting neighbor, and he is not given preference thereby over other neighbors. Likewise if some of the neighbors are partners in the wall, he is not given precedence over other neighbors; because partnership in the mere building without land does not entitle one to pre-emption. If the building and the place on which the building is were shared between them, then he would be more entitled than other neighbors. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/334) 'According to the number of heads': The word 'according to' is attached to His saying: 'It is obligatory for the partner' i.e., pre-emption is obligatory according to the number of heads. And al-Shafi'i said: according to the measure of their shares, and Malik and Ahmad agreed with him. For example, if there is a house among three: one has half, another has one-sixth, and another has one-third. Then the owner of the sixth sells his sixth, and the two others seek pre-emption. It is divided among them in fifths: three fifths for the owner of half, and two fifths for the owner of the third; because pre-emption is among the appurtenances of ownership, so it resembles profit. And our proof: the cause is connection of ownership, and a little of it in that regard is like much of it. So what the owner of the sixth sold is half between them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/335) 'Through sale': It is also attached to His saying: 'It is obligatory for the partner.' And he indicated by this that pre-emption by sale, i.e., selling the house subject to pre-emption, is the cause of obligation; thus said some. And the correct view is that the cause is the connection of properties permanently, and sale is a condition. Then the estimate is: pre-emption is obligatory by the contract of sale, i.e., after its existence. And by 'sale' is meant the valid sale, for pre-emption is not obligatory in a defective sale; because before delivery it does not confer ownership, and after it is subject to rescission, so making it obligatory would confirm the defect, so it is not permissible unless when rescission falls and it becomes obligatory due to removal of the impediment. And in it is another restriction: that it be free from the seller's option; because it prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership, so if he drops it, it becomes obligatory. And the buyer's option is not an impediment because it does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership. Likewise the options of inspection and defect do not prevent. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/335) 'And it is confirmed by bearing witness': i.e., pre-emption is confirmed by bearing witness; because it is a weak right that is nullified by disregard. So bearing witness is necessary after the immediate demand for confirmation, just as the immediate demand is necessary for confirmation – that he demand as soon as he hears. And because he needs to prove his demand before the judge, and he cannot do so except by bearing witness. (Fath)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding pre-emption (shuf'ah). It begins by defining who qualifies as a 'neighbor' (jar) for the purpose of shuf'ah: a person who places his beams on another's wall, or who shares a beam on a wall, is considered a neighbor but not a co-owner. As an abutting neighbor, he is entitled to shuf'ah but does not get priority over other neighbors. The commentary then explains the famous ruling that shuf'ah is distributed among co-owners on the basis of heads, not shares. This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who distributes according to share proportions. The Hanafi proof is that the effective cause ('illa) for shuf'ah is the connection of ownership (ittisal al-milk), and the extent of one's share does not affect this connection. The passage also clarifies that the sale must be valid and free from options that prevent transfer of ownership (like seller's option), while buyer's options do not impede. Finally, it discusses the need for bearing witness (ishhad) to confirm the right of shuf'ah, because it is a weak right that can be lost through negligence.

Key Terms
خيار البائع (khiyār al-bā'iʿ): Seller's option to cancel the sale.
طلب المواثبة (ṭalab al-muwāthaba): Immediate demand upon hearing the sale.
حق ضعيف (ḥaqq ḍaʿīf): Weak right that can be invalidated by negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT prevent the obligation of shuf'ah?
A) The sale is defective (fāsid).
B) The seller has the option to rescind.
C) The buyer has the option to rescind.
D) The pre-emptor fails to demand immediately.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a weak right that becomes obligatory only with a valid sale free from seller's option and is confirmed by immediate demand and bearing witness.

Acquisition and Loss of Pre-emption
Rulings on acquisition and loss of shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of acquiring shuf'ah and identify the three situations that cause loss of the right according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is acquired by consent or court order; lost by death, sale of basis property, or loss of adjacent ownership.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains how the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is actually owned and when it ceases. The matn states two methods of acquisition: by mutual consent with the buyer or by a qadi's judgment. The sharh then adds important rules about loss of the right, emphasizing that shuf'ah is a weak, personal right that does not pass to heirs if the pre-emptor dies before finalizing acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acquisition methods
The text states that shuf'ah is owned by 'taking with mutual consent' (akhdh bil-tarāḍī) or by 'the judgment of the qadi' (qaḍā' al-qāḍī). Note that the qadi's judgment alone vests ownership even without physical taking.
Grammatically, 'bi-qaḍā' al-qāḍī' is attached to 'al-akhdh', not to 'al-tarāḍī'.
2
Understand the effect of the qadi's judgment
The commentator clarifies that the qadi's judgment establishes ownership for the pre-emptor before he actually takes the property. This is because the judgment itself transfers the right.
Taking by qadi's judgment is more precautionary as it records the incident and clarifies the cause of ownership.
3
List the causes of loss of shuf'ah
Three situations cause loss: (1) pre-emptor dies after making the two demands but before delivery or judgment – right not inherited; (2) pre-emptor sells his adjacent property (the basis of his right) – right nullified; (3) the adjacent property is sold to another – pre-emptor loses right due to lack of ownership.
All three involve loss of connection to the adjacent property or failure to finalize before death.
4
Explain why shuf'ah is not inherited
Shuf'ah is a weak personal right. If the pre-emptor dies before final acquisition (by delivery or judgment), the right does not transfer to heirs because it was not fully owned at death.
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it inheritable; Hanafi holds it lapses.
5
Note the precautionary benefit
The commentator notes that taking by qadi's judgment is more precautionary because it creates a clear record and establishes the cause of ownership, avoiding disputes.
This encourages pre-emptors to seek court confirmation even after mutual consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي. وتملك إلخ : أي تملك الشفعة بأخذ الدار المشفوعة بالتراضي، بأن سلمها المشتري برضاه، أو بقضاء القاضي من غير أخذ؛ لأنها ملك، فلا يصح إلا بما ذكرنا. أنه إذا مات الشفيع بعد الطلبين قبل التسليم أو الحكم، لا يورث عنه، ولو باع داره التي يستحق بها الشفعة، بطلت شفعته، ولو بيعت دار بجنبها لا يستحقها بالشفعة؛ لعدم ملكه فيها. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وقال في "الفتح": قوله : "بقضاء القاضي" عطف على "الأخذ" لا على "التراضي"؛ لأن القاضي إذا حكم يثبت الملك للشفيع قبل أخذه يعني يثبت الملك للشفيع بأحد الأمرين: إما بالأخذ بالتراضي أو بحكم الحاكم من غير أخذ، لكن أخذ الشفعة بقضاء القاضي أحوط؛ لأن في القضاء زيادة فائدة، وهو صيرورة الحادثة معلومة للقاضي، وتبيين سبب ملكه له.
And it is owned by taking with mutual consent or by the judgment of the qadi. 'And it is owned etc.': i.e., ownership of shuf'ah is by taking the house subject to shuf'ah with mutual consent, by the buyer surrendering it willingly, or by the judgment of the qadi without taking; because it is ownership, so it is not valid except by what we mentioned. And that if the pre-emptor dies after the two demands before delivery or judgment, it is not inherited from him. And if he sells his house by which he is entitled to shuf'ah, his shuf'ah is nullified. And if a house adjacent to it is sold, he does not deserve shuf'ah due to lack of his ownership in it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/335) And he said in Fath: His saying 'by the judgment of the qadi' is a conjunction to 'taking', not to 'mutual consent'; because when the qadi gives judgment, ownership is established for the pre-emptor before taking. That is, ownership is established for the pre-emptor by one of two matters: either by taking with mutual consent or by the judgment of the ruler without taking. But taking shuf'ah by the qadi's judgment is more precautionary, because in judgment there is increased benefit: it makes the incident known to the qadi and clarifies the cause of his ownership.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on shuf'ah and addresses how the right is actualized. The matn states: 'It is owned by taking with mutual consent or by the judgment of the qadi.' The sharh explains that 'taking' (akhdh) here means the act of the pre-emptor receiving the property either by the buyer willingly surrendering it (mutual consent) or by a court judgment that vests ownership without physical taking. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'by the judgment of the qadi' is grammatically attached to 'taking' and not to 'mutual consent', because the qadi's judgment itself establishes ownership even before physical seizure. The commentary then lists three rulings that cause loss of shuf'ah: (1) If the pre-emptor dies after making the two demands (the immediate demand after hearing of sale and the formal demand for judgment) but before the property is delivered or a judgment is passed, the right of shuf'ah is not inherited. (2) If the pre-emptor sells the property he owns that gave him the right to claim shuf'ah (the property adjacent to the sold one), his claim to shuf'ah is nullified because he no longer has the requisite ownership connection. (3) If the pre-emptor's own property is sold (i.e., the property that was the basis for his shuf'ah claim is sold to someone else), he loses the right to claim shuf'ah because he no longer owns it. These rulings confirm that shuf'ah is a personal right tied to ownership of adjacent property and does not transfer to heirs like normal estate property.

Key Terms
أخذ بالتراضي (akhdh bil-tarāḍī): Taking ownership of the property subject to shuf'ah by the buyer voluntarily surrendering it.
قضاء القاضي (qaḍā' al-qāḍī): The judgment of a qadi that establishes the pre-emptor's ownership even without physical taking.
الطلبين (al-ṭalabayn): The two demands: first demand (upon hearing the sale) and formal demand (for judgment). The pre-emptor must make these demands to preserve his right.
لا يورث (lā yūr ath): It is not inherited; the right of shuf'ah does not pass to heirs upon the pre-emptor's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the pre-emptor dies after making the two demands but before the property is delivered or a judgment is given?
A) The right of shuf'ah passes to his heirs
B) The right of shuf'ah is nullified and not inherited
C) The buyer must hold the property indefinitely
D) The qadi automatically rules in favor of the heirs

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a personal right acquired by mutual consent or court order, but it is lost if the pre-emptor dies before finalization or loses ownership of the adjacent property.

Acquiring Pre-emption by Consent or Court Order
Opening rules on how pre-emption is acquired

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of acquiring pre-emption (shuf'ah) and identify the conditions and consequences of each method according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is owned only by active taking—either by mutual consent or by a judge's ruling.

Pre-emption (shuf'ah) gives a neighbor or co-owner the right to buy a sold property. However, this right does not vest automatically; the pre-emptor must actively exercise it. In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that ownership of the pre-empted property is established either by taking with the buyer's consent or by a court judgment. We also explore the ancillary rulings and the wisdom behind requiring an overt act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acquisition methods
Read the matn: 'وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي'. Identify that ownership is established either by taking with mutual consent of the buyer, or by a judge's ruling.
The word 'أو' indicates a choice between two valid methods.
2
Understand the condition for valid ownership
The commentary explains that pre-emption is a form of ownership (ملك), so it cannot be valid except through one of these two methods. This is a talil (reasoning) that any acquisition requires a valid legal cause.
Ownership must be based on a recognized transfer mechanism.
3
Note the ancillary rulings on death and sale
The text adds: if the pre-emptor dies after making the two demands but before delivery or judgment, the right is not inherited. Also, if he sells his adjoining property, his pre-emption right is voided. Recognize these as conditions that either prevent inheritance or extinguish the right.
The two demands (talab al-muwathabah and talab al-taqrir) are prerequisites for the right to mature.
4
Appreciate the extra benefit of court ruling
The commentary from al-Fath notes that 'بقضاء القاضي' is attached to 'الأخذ' not to 'التراضي', because a judge's ruling establishes ownership without physical taking. Court order is more cautious (أحوط) as it creates a public record and clarifies the cause of ownership.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on legal certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
مسائل الشفعة
وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي أو بقضاء القاضي.
الشفعة
وتملك إلخ : أي تملك الشفعة بأخذ الدار المشفوعة بالتراضي، بأن سلمها المشتري برضاه، أو بقضاء القاضي من غير أخذ؛ لأنها ملك، فلا يصح إلا بما ذكرنا.
أنه إذا مات الشفيع بعد الطلبين قبل التسليم أو الحكم، لا يورث عنه، ولو باع داره التي يستحق بها
الشفعة، بطلت شفعته، ولو بيعت دار بجنبها لا يستحقها بالشفعة؛ لعدم ملكه فيها.
[رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٥/٢] وقال في "الفتح": قوله : "بقضاء القاضي" عطف على "الأخذ" لا على التراضي"؛ لأن القاضي إذا حكم يثبت الملك للشفيع قبل أخذه يعني يثبت الملك للشفيع بأحد الأمرين: إما بالأخذ بالتراضي أو بحكم الحاكم من غير أخذ، لكن أخذ الشفعة بقضاء القاضي أحوط؛ لأن في القضاء زيادة فائدة، وهو صيرورة الحادثة معلومة للقاضي، وتبين سبب ملكه له.
Book of Pre-emption. Rules of Pre-emption. And it is owned by taking by mutual consent or by the judgment of the judge. Commentary: 'And it is owned etc.' meaning: ownership of the pre-empted property is established by taking by mutual consent, such that the buyer hands it over willingly, or by the judgment of the judge without taking, because it is ownership, so it is not valid except as we have mentioned. That if the pre-emptor dies after the two demands before delivery or judgment, it is not inherited from him. And if he sells his house by which he is entitled to pre-emption, his pre-emption is void. And if a house next to it is sold, he is not entitled to it by pre-emption because he has no ownership in it. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 335/2] And it is said in al-Fath: His statement 'by the judgment of the judge' is a conjunction to 'taking' not to 'mutual consent', because when the judge rules, ownership is established for the pre-emptor before his taking. That is, ownership is established for the pre-emptor by one of two things: either by taking by mutual consent or by the judge's ruling without taking. But taking pre-emption by the judge's ruling is more cautious, because in the ruling there is an added benefit: the incident becomes known to the judge and the cause of his ownership is clarified.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the acquisition of pre-emption. The author states that the pre-emptor becomes owner of the pre-empted property through one of two means: either by taking it with the mutual consent of the buyer (i.e., the buyer voluntarily surrenders the property), or by the judgment of a judge. The commentator explains that the ruling is because pre-emption is a form of ownership; thus it cannot be valid except by one of these two methods. The text then notes two additional rulings: (1) If the pre-emptor dies after making the two demands (talab al-muwathabah and talab al-taqrir) but before the property is delivered or a court ruling is issued, the right of pre-emption is not inherited by his heirs. (2) If the pre-emptor sells the property that gave him the right of pre-emption (e.g., the adjoining house), his pre-emption right is nullified. Also, if a house next to his is sold, he does not acquire pre-emption right in it if he has no legal ownership relationship (such as being a co-owner or adjoining neighbor with right of shuf'ah). The commentator in al-Fath clarifies the grammatical point: 'bi qada' al-qadi' is conjuncted to 'al-akhdh', not to 'al-taradi', because the judge's ruling establishes ownership before actual taking, while mutual consent requires actual taking. He advises that taking pre-emption by court order is more precautionary as it creates a public record.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption; the option to purchase a sold property that adjoins one's own or in which one has a share of the right of way.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption; the pre-emptor.
التراضي (al-taradi): Mutual consent between the buyer and the pre-emptor regarding the transfer of the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is ownership of the pre-empted property established according to the matn?
A) Automatically upon the sale of the adjoining property.
B) By taking with mutual consent or by the judgment of a judge.
C) Only by a court order.
D) By paying the price to the original seller.

Key Takeaway
Pre-emption is owned only by taking with mutual consent or by court judgment; it is not automatic.

Demand for Pre-emption: The Obligation of Immediate Demand
Detailed rulings on demand for pre-emption including conditions for its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the demand of pre-emption and distinguish the three types of demand.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is forfeited by delay; immediate demand upon knowledge is essential.

The demand for pre-emption is not merely a formality but a legal requirement that must be fulfilled promptly. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the conditions of the first demand, the effect of different informants, and the types of demand. It also highlights a key dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding who qualifies as an informant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on demand
The pre-emptor must bear witness immediately upon learning of the sale in the same sitting. Delay or silence voids the right.
This is the first type of demand: talab al-muwathabah.
2
Analyze the informant qualification dispute
Compare Imam Abu Hanifa's requirement (two non-just men, or one just man, or one man and two women) with the Sahibayn's view (any truthful informant, even a slave or minor).
The dispute affects when the demand becomes obligatory.
3
Understand the effect of speech and silence
Certain utterances like 'alhamdulillah' do not indicate rejection, and coerced silence does not void the right.
The key is whether the pre-emptor's behavior indicates acceptance of the new neighbor.
4
Distinguish the three types of demand
Talab al-muwathabah (immediate), talab al-taqrir (confirmatory to seller), talab al-tamalluk (before judge).
Only the first is discussed in this passage.

كتاب الشفعة ٢٦٨ طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها باب طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها فإن علم الشفيع بالبيع أشهد في مجلسه على الطلب، شرط أي بيع مجلس علمه الدار المشفوعة باب طلب الشفعة إلخ لما لم تثبت الشفعة بدون الطلب، شرع بيانه وكيفيته وتقسيمه، وزاد في "الهداية": قوله: "والخصومة فيها، ووجهه أنه لما كان للخصومة في الشفعة شأن مخصوص، وتفاصيل زائدة على سائر الخصومات شرع في بيانها. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٥٤/٨] فإن علم إلخ بأن أخبره رجلان، أو رجل وامرأتان، أو واحد عدل عند الإمام وعندهما بخبر واحد، ولو عبدا صغيرا إذا كان الخبر حقا، ولو أخبره المشتري يجب عليه الطلب بالإجماع كيف ما كان؛ لأنه خصم، والعدالة في الخصوم غير معتبرة. (كذا في العيني) أشهد إلخ: أي أشهد على نفسه على الفور من غير تأخير ولا سكوت في مجلسه على الطلب؛ لأن سكوته بعد العلم يدل على رضاه بجوار الجار الحادث ومعاشرته فتبطل به الشفعة إذا كان بعد العلم بالمشتري والثمن، ولو أخبر بكتاب والشفعة في أوله أو في أوسطه فقرأ الكتاب إلى آخره بلا طلب بطلت شفعته؛ لتأخير الطلب، فإن أخبر بحضرة الشهود يشهدهم عليه وإلا يطلب من غير إشهاد؛ لأن هذا الطلب صحيح من غير إشهاد، ويشترط أن يكون متصلا بعلمه عند عامة المشايخ، وهو مروي عن محمد وعنه أن له التأمل إلى آخر المجلس كالمخيرة، وبهذا أخذ الكرخي. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٦/٢] ولو سكت مكرها لا تبطل، ويصح الطلب بكل لفظ يفهم منه الطلب في الحال، ولا يجب الطلب حتى يخبره رجلان غير عدلين أو رجل عدل، أو رجل وامرأتان؛ لأنه فيه التزام من وجه فيشترط له أحد شطري الشهادة، هذا قول الإمام. وعندهما يجب عليه الطلب إذا أخبره واحد حرا كان أو عبدا ، صغيرا كان أو كبيرا، إذا كان الخبر حقا، ولو أخبره المشتري بنفسه يجب عليه الطلب بالإجماع كيفما كان، ولو قال بعد ما علم البيع: الحمد الله، أو لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم، أو سبحان الله، لا تبطل به شفعته على ما اختاره الكرخي؛ لأن الأول حمد على الخلاص، والثاني تعجب، والثالث افتتاح الكلام، ولا يدل شيء منها على الإعراض، وكذا إذا قال: من ابتاعها، أو بكم بيعت؛ لأنه يرغب فيها ثمن دون ثمن، وكذا لو قال: خلصني الله. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٥٤/٨] في مجلسه: أي أشهد على نفسه في مجلسه سواء كان عنده أحد أو لم يكن قال الأقطع: وإنما يفعل ذلك، وإن لم يكن عنده أحد؛ لئلا يسقط حقه ديانة، وفي "المبسوط": لكي يتمكن من الحلف إذا حلفه المشتري، ولا حاجة في هذا الطلب إلى الإشهاد ؛ لأن الإشهاد لمخافة الجحود. (فتح). على الطلب : اعلم أن الطلب في الشفعة ينقسم إلى ثلاثة طلب مواثبة وطلب تقرير وطلب تملك، وهذا المذكور هو القسم الأول أي طلب المواثبة، وإنما سمي طلب المواثبة؛ لقوله عليه: "الشفعة لمن واثبها " أي طلبها على وجه السرعة والمبادرة، والقسم الثاني: ما أشار إليه بقوله: "ثم على البائع" إلخ، والثالث: ما أشار إليه بقوله: "فإن طلب عند القاضي" إلخ. (تكملة، فتح)
Book of Pre-emption 268. Demand for Pre-emption and Litigation concerning it. Chapter of Demand for Pre-emption and Litigation concerning it. If the pre-emptor learns of the sale, he must bear witness in his sitting to the demand, as a condition... etc. (Commentary:) ... The demand in pre-emption is divided into three: demand of al-muwathabah (immediate demand), demand of al-taqrir (affirmation), and demand of al-tamalluk (taking possession). This mentioned is the first section, i.e. demand of al-muwathabah, and it is named demand of al-muwathabah because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Pre-emption belongs to the one who makes a swift demand' i.e. demands it with speed and promptness. The second section is what he indicated by his statement: 'then upon the seller' etc. The third is what he indicated by his statement: 'if he demands before the judge' etc.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq elaborates the conditions for the demand (talab) of pre-emption. The main ruling is that upon learning of the sale, the pre-emptor must immediately make a demand in that same sitting and bring witnesses to it; otherwise, silence after knowledge indicates satisfaction with the new neighbor and voids his right. The commentator clarifies who counts as a valid informant of the sale: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, two non-just men, or one just man, or a man and two women are required for the obligation to demand; while the Sahibayn hold that even a single informant (free or slave, minor or adult) obligates the demand if the information is true. The text also discusses the effect of various utterances after hearing the news (e.g., 'alhamdulillah', 'la hawla' etc.)—they do not void the right according to al-Karkhi because they do not indicate rejection. Finally, the passage divides the demand into three types: (1) talab al-muwathabah (immediate demand), which is the first demand upon hearing the news; (2) talab al-taqrir (confirmatory demand) addressed to the seller; and (3) talab al-tamalluk (demand for possession) addressed to the judge. This first type is named after the hadith 'al-shuf'atu liman wathabaha' (pre-emption is for the one who makes a swift demand).

Key Terms
طلب المواثبة (talab al-muwathabah): The immediate demand upon hearing the sale; the first of three types of demand in shuf'ah.
طلب التقرير (talab al-taqrir): The confirmatory demand addressed to the seller, affirming the pre-emptor's right.
طلب التملك (talab al-tamalluk): The demand for possession addressed to the judge to take ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence if the pre-emptor remains silent after being informed of the sale?
A) His pre-emption right is strengthened.
B) His pre-emption right is voided because silence indicates consent.
C) Nothing; he can demand later.
D) He must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
The demand for pre-emption must be made immediately upon learning of the sale; otherwise, silence may indicate consent and forfeit the right.

Proper Parties and Evidence in Pre-emption Litigation
Distinguishing litigants and procedural evidence requirements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish who qualifies as a proper litigant for the pre-emptor and state the procedural requirement for hearing evidence and rescission.

Core Idea
Only the seller with original possession is a proper litigant; the buyer must be present for rescission before delivery.

In pre-emption litigation, not every person in possession of the property can be sued. The Hanafi school distinguishes between original and derivative possession. This lesson clarifies whom the pre-emptor may litigate with and the procedural steps required for the judge to hear the case and rescind the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Possessor
Determine who has physical possession of the property. Is it the seller, a depositary, a borrower, or someone else?
2
Classify the Type of Possession
Is the possession original (asālah) or derivative? The seller has original possession and is a proper litigant; a depositary or borrower has only derivative possession and is not a litigant.
Original possession means the person holds the property in his own right, not as a trustee.
3
Examine the Evidence Requirement
The judge does not hear the pre-emptor's evidence until the buyer is present, because both seller and buyer have rights in the property: seller has possession, buyer has ownership.
The pre-emptor's claim affects both rights.
4
Distinguish Before vs After Delivery
Before delivery, the buyer must be present for rescission. After delivery, the seller is no longer a party, so his presence is not required.
After delivery, the contract has ended and the seller becomes a stranger to the dispute.

Source Text

وخاصم البائع إلخ يعني للشفيع أن يخاصم البائع إذا كان المبيع في يده؛ لأن له يدا محقة أصالة، فكان خصما كالمالك، بخلاف المودع والمستعير ونحوهما؛ لأن يدهم ليست أصالة، فلا يكون خصما تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٥٩/٨] ولا يسمع البينة حتى يحضر المشتري، فيفسخ البيع بمشهده، والعهدة على البائع، والوكيل بالشراء خصم للشفيع ما لم يسلّم إلى الموكل، وللشفيع خيار الرؤية والعيب، وإن شرط المشتري البراءة منه، وإن اختلف الشفيع والمشتري في الثمن. (عيني) ولا يسمع البينة إلخ أي لا يسمع القاضي البينة حتى يحضر المشتري؛ لأن لكل منهما في المبيع حقا، للبائع اليد وللمشتري الملك، والشفيع يتعرض للحقين جميعا، فلابد من حضورهما [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۸/۲] فيفسخ البيع إلخ : أي فيفسخ القاضي البيع بمشهد المشتري وحضوره، بخلاف ما بعد القبض حيث لا يشترط حضور البائع؛ لأن العقد قد انتهى بالتسليم، فصار البائع أجنبيا عنهما. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳٨/٢] والعهدة على البائع إلخ: أي ضمان الثمن عند الاستحقاق على البائع عندنا أي قبل تسليم البيع إلى المشتري، وقالت الثلاثة على المشتري، والأصل في ذلك أن حقوق العقد ترجع إلى المالك عندهم، وإلى العاقد عندنا. (عيني، فتح) والوكيل بالشراء إلخ [ إذا وكل رجلا ليشتري له دارا فاشترى فالوكيل خصم للشفيع. (ملا مسكين)] فلا يشترط للقضاء حضور الموكل ولا كذلك البائع؛ لأنه ليس بنائب عن المشتري، فلا يكتفي بحضوره، بخلاف الوكيل والأب ووصيه كالوكيل. (فتح) ما لم يسلم إلى الموكل: أي الوكيل بالشراء خصم للشفيع ما لم يسلم إلى الموكل؛ لأن الخصومة فيه من حقوق العقد، وهي إلى العاقد أصيلا كان أو وكيلا، ولهذا لو كان البائع و وكيلا للشفيع أن يخاصمه، ويأخذها منه بحضور المشتري، كما إذا كان البائع هو المالك إلا أنه إذا سلمها إلى الموكل، لا يد للوكيل، ولا ملك له، ولا يكون خصما بعده، فصار كالبائع، فإنه يكون خصما ما لم يسلمه إلى المشتري، فإذا سلمها إليه لم يبق له يد، ولا ملك، فيخرج من أن يكون خصما تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٠/٨] وعند الثلاثة الخصم هو الموكل ابتداء؛ لأن الوكيل بمنزلة السفير. [ رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٨/۲] وفي "التاتارخانية": لو اشترى لغيره بغير أمره، فهو خصم ما لم يسلم العين إلى من اشتراها له، فلو قال المؤلف: "والمشتري لغيره خصم ما لم يسلم لكان أولى تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٠/٨] وللشفيع خيار الرؤية إلخ أي يثبت للشفيع خيار الرؤية، وخيار العيب وإن شرط المشتري البراءة من العيب، وهذا بالإجماع؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة شراء من المشتري إن كان الأخذ بعد القبض، وإن كان قبله فهو من البائع، فيثبت له الخيار تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦١/٨] ولا يسقط الخيار برؤية المشتري، وبشرط براءته؛ لأن الشفيع ليس بنائب عنه، فلا يسقط حقه بإسقاط المشتري. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۸/۲] وإن اختلف إلخ أي إذا اختلف الشفيع والمشتري في مقدار الثمن، فقال الشفيع اشتريتها بمائة، وقال المشتري: اشتريتها بمائة وعشرين، فالقول للمشتري؛ لأن الشفيع يدعي عليه استحقاق الأخذ عند نقد الأقل، والمشتري ينكر ذلك، والقول للمنكر مع يمينه ولا يتحالفان؛ لأن التحالف عرف بالنص فيما إذا وجد الإنكار الجانبين.
'And he litigates with the seller etc.': meaning the pre-emptor may litigate with the seller if the sold property is in his hand, because he has a rightful possession originally, so he is a litigant like the owner, unlike the depositary and borrower and similar, because their possession is not original, so they are not litigants. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/259) 'And the evidence is not heard until the buyer is present, then the sale is rescinded in his presence, and the liability (for the price) is on the seller, and the agent in purchase is a litigant for the pre-emptor as long as he has not delivered to the principal, and the pre-emptor has the option of sight and defect, even if the buyer stipulated exemption from defect, and if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute over the price.' (Ayni) 'And the evidence is not heard etc.': meaning the judge does not hear the evidence until the buyer is present, because each of them has a right in the sold property: the seller has possession and the buyer has ownership, and the pre-emptor is contesting both rights, so their presence is necessary. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'Then the sale is rescinded etc.': meaning the judge rescinds the sale in the presence and attendance of the buyer, unlike after delivery where the seller's presence is not required, because the contract has ended with delivery, so the seller has become a stranger to them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'And the liability is on the seller etc.': meaning the guarantee of the price upon eviction is on the seller in our view (i.e., before delivery of the sale to the buyer), and the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Shafi'i) say it is on the buyer. The basis is that rights of the contract revert to the owner according to them, and to the contractor according to us. (Ayni, Fath) 'And the agent in purchase etc.': [if a man appoints an agent to buy a house for him and he buys it, the agent is a litigant for the pre-emptor. (Mulla Miskin)] So the presence of the principal is not required for judgment, nor is the seller; because he is not a representative of the buyer, so his presence is not sufficient, unlike the agent, the father, and his executor, who are like the agent. (Fath) 'As long as he has not delivered to the principal': meaning the agent in purchase is a litigant for the pre-emptor as long as he has not delivered to the principal, because the litigation is among the rights of the contract, and it pertains to the contractor, whether he is an original or an agent. For this reason, if the seller is an agent, the pre-emptor may litigate with him and take it from him in the presence of the buyer, just as if the seller were the owner. But if he delivers it to the principal, the agent has no possession or ownership, and he is not a litigant after that, so he becomes like the seller: he is a litigant as long as he has not delivered to the buyer; when he delivers to him, he no longer has possession or ownership, so he leaves being a litigant. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/260) And according to the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Shafi'i), the litigant is the principal from the beginning, because the agent is like a messenger. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If someone buys for another without his order, he is a litigant until he delivers the property to the one for whom he bought it. So if the author said: 'And the buyer for another is a litigant until he delivers', it would be more appropriate. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/260) 'And the pre-emptor has the option of sight etc.': meaning the pre-emptor has the option of sight and the option of defect, even if the buyer stipulated exemption from defect, and this is by consensus, because taking by pre-emption is a purchase from the buyer if the taking is after delivery, and if before delivery it is from the seller, so he has the option. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/261) And the option is not voided by the buyer's sight or by his stipulation of exemption, because the pre-emptor is not his representative, so his right is not voided by the buyer's waiver. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'And if they dispute etc.': meaning if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute over the amount of the price, and the pre-emptor says: You bought it for one hundred, and the buyer says: I bought it for one hundred and twenty, the buyer's statement is accepted, because the pre-emptor claims the right to take upon paying the lower amount, and the buyer denies that; the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath, and they do not both swear, because mutual oaths (tahaluf) are established by the text only when denial comes from both sides.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on Kitab al-Shuf'ah from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering several distinct rulings. First, the pre-emptor may also litigate with the seller directly if the property is still in the seller's possession, because the seller has an original right of possession. This is different from a depositary or borrower, who have only derivative possession and thus are not proper litigants. Second, the judge does not hear the pre-emptor's evidence unless the buyer is present, because both the seller and buyer have rights in the property. After the buyer is present, the judge rescinds the sale. If the property has already been delivered to the buyer, the seller's presence is not required. Third, the liability for the price (al-uhdah) – i.e., if the pre-emptor's ownership is later invalidated, who must return the price? According to the Hanafi school, before delivery, the liability is on the seller, because the contract's rights are with the contracting party. The 'three' (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i) hold that liability is on the buyer, because rights revert to the owner. This is a significant inter-madhhab dispute. Fourth, an agent who buys for a principal is a proper litigant for the pre-emptor as long as the agent has not delivered the property to the principal. After delivery, the principal becomes the litigant. This is because the agent is the actual contractor. The opposing view (the three) holds that the principal is the litigant from the start, as the agent is merely a messenger. Fifth, the pre-emptor has the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) and option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), even if the buyer had stipulated exemption from defects. This is by consensus, because the pre-emptor is taking by a new purchase, so he has the same options as any buyer. His options are not affected by the buyer's actions. Sixth, if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute the price, the buyer's word is taken with an oath, because he is the denier of the pre-emptor's claim. They do not both swear (tahaluf) because mutual oaths are only for cases where both parties deny each other's claims.

Key Terms
عهدة (uhdah): Liability for the price in case of eviction or invalidity of the sale.
وكيل بالشراء (wakil bil-shira'): An agent appointed specifically to purchase a property on behalf of a principal.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option to confirm or rescind a contract after seeing the object of sale, if the buyer had not previously seen it.
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they dispute a contract and both are unable to provide evidence.
مودع (mūda‘): Depositary – a person with whom property is deposited for safekeeping.
مستعير (musta‘īr): Borrower – one who borrows an item for use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is considered a proper litigant for the pre-emptor when the sold property is still in the seller's hand?
A) The seller
B) The depositary
C) The borrower
D) The neighbor

Key Takeaway
Only the seller (as original possessor) is a litigant before delivery; the buyer must be present for the judge to hear evidence and rescind the sale.

Liability for the Price (al-Uhdah) – Hanafi Doctrine vs. Others
The dispute over liability for the price in pre-emption before delivery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that before delivery, liability for the price is on the seller, and evaluate the opposing view of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Rights of the contract revert to the contractor; thus liability for the price is on the seller until delivery, not the owner.

In pre-emption, if the pre-emptor's ownership is later invalidated (e.g., due to a prior right), a dispute arises over who must return the price to the pre-emptor: the seller or the buyer? The Hanafi school takes a distinctive position based on the usul principle that contractual rights belong to the contracting party. This lesson unpacks that dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
When the pre-emptor's right fails before delivery, who bears the 'uhdah (guarantee of the price)?
The dispute is specifically about the period before delivery of the property to the buyer.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school holds that liability is on the seller, because the contract's rights revert to the contractor (al-‘āqid).
The seller is the one who entered the contract.
3
State the Opposing Position
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i hold that liability is on the buyer, because rights revert to the owner (al-mālik).
The buyer becomes the owner after the sale.
4
Analyze the Basis
The difference stems from a usul dispute: do rights follow the contractor or the owner? Hanafi: contractor; others: owner.
This is a foundational principle affecting many branches of fiqh.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
If the pre-emptor loses his claim, he recovers the price from the seller (Hanafi) or from the buyer (opposing).
This affects whom the pre-emptor sues for recovery.

وخاصم البائع إلخ يعني للشفيع أن يخاصم البائع إذا كان المبيع في يده؛ لأن له يدا محقة أصالة، فكان خصما كالمالك، بخلاف المودع والمستعير ونحوهما؛ لأن يدهم ليست أصالة، فلا يكون خصما تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٥٩/٨] ولا يسمع البينة حتى يحضر المشتري، فيفسخ البيع بمشهده، والعهدة على البائع، والوكيل بالشراء خصم للشفيع ما لم يسلّم إلى الموكل، وللشفيع خيار الرؤية والعيب، وإن شرط المشتري البراءة منه، وإن اختلف الشفيع والمشتري في الثمن. (عيني) ولا يسمع البينة إلخ أي لا يسمع القاضي البينة حتى يحضر المشتري؛ لأن لكل منهما في المبيع حقا، للبائع اليد وللمشتري الملك، والشفيع يتعرض للحقين جميعا، فلابد من حضورهما [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۸/۲] فيفسخ البيع إلخ : أي فيفسخ القاضي البيع بمشهد المشتري وحضوره، بخلاف ما بعد القبض حيث لا يشترط حضور البائع؛ لأن العقد قد انتهى بالتسليم، فصار البائع أجنبيا عنهما. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳٨/٢] والعهدة على البائع إلخ: أي ضمان الثمن عند الاستحقاق على البائع عندنا أي قبل تسليم البيع إلى المشتري، وقالت الثلاثة على المشتري، والأصل في ذلك أن حقوق العقد ترجع إلى المالك عندهم، وإلى العاقد عندنا. (عيني، فتح) والوكيل بالشراء إلخ [ إذا وكل رجلا ليشتري له دارا فاشترى فالوكيل خصم للشفيع. (ملا مسكين)] فلا يشترط للقضاء حضور الموكل ولا كذلك البائع؛ لأنه ليس بنائب عن المشتري، فلا يكتفي بحضوره، بخلاف الوكيل والأب ووصيه كالوكيل. (فتح) ما لم يسلم إلى الموكل: أي الوكيل بالشراء خصم للشفيع ما لم يسلم إلى الموكل؛ لأن الخصومة فيه من حقوق العقد، وهي إلى العاقد أصيلا كان أو وكيلا، ولهذا لو كان البائع و وكيلا للشفيع أن يخاصمه، ويأخذها منه بحضور المشتري، كما إذا كان البائع هو المالك إلا أنه إذا سلمها إلى الموكل، لا يد للوكيل، ولا ملك له، ولا يكون خصما بعده، فصار كالبائع، فإنه يكون خصما ما لم يسلمه إلى المشتري، فإذا سلمها إليه لم يبق له يد، ولا ملك، فيخرج من أن يكون خصما تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٠/٨] وعند الثلاثة الخصم هو الموكل ابتداء؛ لأن الوكيل بمنزلة السفير. [ رمز الحقائق: ٣٣٨/۲] وفي "التاتارخانية": لو اشترى لغيره بغير أمره، فهو خصم ما لم يسلم العين إلى من اشتراها له، فلو قال المؤلف: "والمشتري لغيره خصم ما لم يسلم لكان أولى تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦٠/٨] وللشفيع خيار الرؤية إلخ أي يثبت للشفيع خيار الرؤية، وخيار العيب وإن شرط المشتري البراءة من العيب، وهذا بالإجماع؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة شراء من المشتري إن كان الأخذ بعد القبض، وإن كان قبله فهو من البائع، فيثبت له الخيار تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٦١/٨] ولا يسقط الخيار برؤية المشتري، وبشرط براءته؛ لأن الشفيع ليس بنائب عنه، فلا يسقط حقه بإسقاط المشتري. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۸/۲] وإن اختلف إلخ أي إذا اختلف الشفيع والمشتري في مقدار الثمن، فقال الشفيع اشتريتها بمائة، وقال المشتري: اشتريتها بمائة وعشرين، فالقول للمشتري؛ لأن الشفيع يدعي عليه استحقاق الأخذ عند نقد الأقل، والمشتري ينكر ذلك، والقول للمنكر مع يمينه ولا يتحالفان؛ لأن التحالف عرف بالنص فيما إذا وجد الإنكار الجانبين.
'And he litigates with the seller etc.': meaning the pre-emptor may litigate with the seller if the sold property is in his hand, because he has a rightful possession originally, so he is a litigant like the owner, unlike the depositary and borrower and similar, because their possession is not original, so they are not litigants. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/259) 'And the evidence is not heard until the buyer is present, then the sale is rescinded in his presence, and the liability (for the price) is on the seller, and the agent in purchase is a litigant for the pre-emptor as long as he has not delivered to the principal, and the pre-emptor has the option of sight and defect, even if the buyer stipulated exemption from defect, and if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute over the price.' (Ayni) 'And the evidence is not heard etc.': meaning the judge does not hear the evidence until the buyer is present, because each of them has a right in the sold property: the seller has possession and the buyer has ownership, and the pre-emptor is contesting both rights, so their presence is necessary. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'Then the sale is rescinded etc.': meaning the judge rescinds the sale in the presence and attendance of the buyer, unlike after delivery where the seller's presence is not required, because the contract has ended with delivery, so the seller has become a stranger to them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'And the liability is on the seller etc.': meaning the guarantee of the price upon eviction is on the seller in our view (i.e., before delivery of the sale to the buyer), and the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Shafi'i) say it is on the buyer. The basis is that rights of the contract revert to the owner according to them, and to the contractor according to us. (Ayni, Fath) 'And the agent in purchase etc.': [if a man appoints an agent to buy a house for him and he buys it, the agent is a litigant for the pre-emptor. (Mulla Miskin)] So the presence of the principal is not required for judgment, nor is the seller; because he is not a representative of the buyer, so his presence is not sufficient, unlike the agent, the father, and his executor, who are like the agent. (Fath) 'As long as he has not delivered to the principal': meaning the agent in purchase is a litigant for the pre-emptor as long as he has not delivered to the principal, because the litigation is among the rights of the contract, and it pertains to the contractor, whether he is an original or an agent. For this reason, if the seller is an agent, the pre-emptor may litigate with him and take it from him in the presence of the buyer, just as if the seller were the owner. But if he delivers it to the principal, the agent has no possession or ownership, and he is not a litigant after that, so he becomes like the seller: he is a litigant as long as he has not delivered to the buyer; when he delivers to him, he no longer has possession or ownership, so he leaves being a litigant. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/260) And according to the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Shafi'i), the litigant is the principal from the beginning, because the agent is like a messenger. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If someone buys for another without his order, he is a litigant until he delivers the property to the one for whom he bought it. So if the author said: 'And the buyer for another is a litigant until he delivers', it would be more appropriate. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/260) 'And the pre-emptor has the option of sight etc.': meaning the pre-emptor has the option of sight and the option of defect, even if the buyer stipulated exemption from defect, and this is by consensus, because taking by pre-emption is a purchase from the buyer if the taking is after delivery, and if before delivery it is from the seller, so he has the option. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/261) And the option is not voided by the buyer's sight or by his stipulation of exemption, because the pre-emptor is not his representative, so his right is not voided by the buyer's waiver. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 3/338] 'And if they dispute etc.': meaning if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute over the amount of the price, and the pre-emptor says: You bought it for one hundred, and the buyer says: I bought it for one hundred and twenty, the buyer's statement is accepted, because the pre-emptor claims the right to take upon paying the lower amount, and the buyer denies that; the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath, and they do not both swear, because mutual oaths (tahaluf) are established by the text only when denial comes from both sides.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on Kitab al-Shuf'ah from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering several distinct rulings. First, the pre-emptor may also litigate with the seller directly if the property is still in the seller's possession, because the seller has an original right of possession. This is different from a depositary or borrower, who have only derivative possession and thus are not proper litigants. Second, the judge does not hear the pre-emptor's evidence unless the buyer is present, because both the seller and buyer have rights in the property. After the buyer is present, the judge rescinds the sale. If the property has already been delivered to the buyer, the seller's presence is not required. Third, the liability for the price (al-uhdah) – i.e., if the pre-emptor's ownership is later invalidated, who must return the price? According to the Hanafi school, before delivery, the liability is on the seller, because the contract's rights are with the contracting party. The 'three' (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i) hold that liability is on the buyer, because rights revert to the owner. This is a significant inter-madhhab dispute. Fourth, an agent who buys for a principal is a proper litigant for the pre-emptor as long as the agent has not delivered the property to the principal. After delivery, the principal becomes the litigant. This is because the agent is the actual contractor. The opposing view (the three) holds that the principal is the litigant from the start, as the agent is merely a messenger. Fifth, the pre-emptor has the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) and option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), even if the buyer had stipulated exemption from defects. This is by consensus, because the pre-emptor is taking by a new purchase, so he has the same options as any buyer. His options are not affected by the buyer's actions. Sixth, if the pre-emptor and buyer dispute the price, the buyer's word is taken with an oath, because he is the denier of the pre-emptor's claim. They do not both swear (tahaluf) because mutual oaths are only for cases where both parties deny each other's claims.

Key Terms
عهدة (uhdah): Liability for the price in case of eviction or invalidity of the sale.
عاقد ('āqid): Contracting party – the person who actually enters the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who bears liability for the price (al-‘uhdah) in pre-emption before delivery?
A) The buyer
B) The seller
C) Both equally
D) The pre-emptor himself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability for the price before delivery is on the seller because contractual rights belong to the contractor.
